fileContents = defaultdict(list)
with open('tripadvisor_royalflora.csv',encoding='utf-8') as f:
    reader = csv.DictReader(f)
    
    for row in reader: # read a row as {column1: value1, column2: value2,...}
        for (k,v) in row.items(): # go over each column name and value 
            fileContents[k].append(v) # append the value

 'This is a great place to spend a few hours taking in the various gardens and views. The admission is very reasonable and it is only about 10 kilometers from the city of Chiang Mai. We negotiated a fare of 180 baht for two people to ride a tuk-tuk from the city. Once there you can walk around if you want some exercise or take the tram. Bring a good hat for the strong sun on clear days and walking shoes. We found this place to be well worth the trip as it is spacious and does not feel like a tourist trap like so many other attractions in Chiang Mai. We went in mid-February which is towards the tail end of the flower season and I am not sure what the place is like at other times of the year.',

This dual pricing is commonplace in Thailand but for the experience you will have, it's extremely cheap. \nThe best way of getting around is by using the shuttle bus which allows you to hop on and  hop off at different places within the gardens.  'Royal Park Rajapruek\nThe Royal Park Rajapruek was laid out in 2006 in Chiang Mai, Thailand, to commemorate the 60th anniversary of His Majesty the King Bhumibol Adulyadejs Accession to the throne as well as His Majesty 80th birthday. About 12 km away from city center, this large floral and botanical park has thousands of plants and flowers and a nice orchids garden. Opened for public in 2008, the Park is spread over about 200 acres land at the foot of Doi Suthep hill. There is a tram service to go around the park. It is a beautiful park with a number of small gardens and pavilions. Particularly the Royal Pavilion in the center of the park is simply stunning. The park has some very peaceful portions for those who love to spend some time in the lap of mother nature.',
 'This is one of our favorite places in Chiang Mai.  We return here over and over, especially if we have guest in town, or for the months of the flower festival.  We bring our bikes (though you can rent nice bikes there very cheap) and leisurely ride around the exhibits, and enjoy all the flowers and beautiful gardens.  The "temple" in the center of the park is lovely and the photo ops abound.  If you are not interested in biking, you can take the tram all around and hop on and off where you want, for a nominal fee.\n\nI would not recommend going here if it is extremely hot.  It\'s best in the morning before the heat and humidity take hold of the day.  The flowers and gardens are most impressive in December and January (maybe February) when the flower festival goes on.',

 'Ratchapruek Royal Park is a good half-hour drive from Chiang Mai. Admission is 100 baht. What you get is a planned garden -- it\'s large -- with three distinct parts. \n\nThe first is a floral display. There is a good section of orchids (though I have seen better orchid gardens in other cities), and a cool greenhouse with tulips and other temperate plants.\n\nThe second is a collection of faux "national" buildings and associated gardens, representing China, Japan, etc. Kitsch.\n\nThe third is the mandatory centrepiece of a Thai building set majestically on a rise, surrounded by a reflecting pool, metal umbrellas and other grandiloquent paraphernalia of national glory...\n\nGo only if such plasticky displays interest you.',

 "My bike ride through the big city was easier, safer, and more comfortable than other countries and cities I've faced, thanks in part to some wide highways having only light to moderate traffic.  You could do the same if you're up for the outdoor activity and exercise.  From Chang Klan, east of the old city, I made a 13k southen loop via 4032, 3029, and 121 to the park, and returned with a 15k northern loop via 121, Suthep, and old town.  With 4 hours touring the park, this made for a tiring day - but a good one I'd recommend for anyone wanting an outdoor activity.  Inside the metro area is not the best biking to be found of course, but if you want to ride, get some exercise, and enjoy a park visit, consider this an attractive option.  Don't try to do it on a 50B junker though.  Find yourself a decent road, hybrid, or mountain bike.  I found NK Bike Rentals offering the best value mountain bikes for 250B/day + 1000B deposit & copy of passport.\n\nEntry into the park is 200B per person plus 20B for the bike.  For those wanting to ride a bike around the park but skip the extra 28k commute, you can do so.  They rent them, and I may have seen the price at 60B/hr?  Here, you'll get basic rides, but sufficient for the purpose.  Whether you bring your own or rent one there, I'd propose that touring the park with a bike is the best way to go - if you're physically up to riding a 2-wheeler.  I noticed most people walking and/or using the free local train transports.  Now if you just want to zip through the park in an hour and see the main arenas, this is fine; but if you want to see the whole park and cover the many side streets and outdoor displays, you'll have more walking to do than most people would want.  Being a walker myself, I was still glad to be on wheels, where I was able to cover virtually every street and all of the displays with ease and pleasure.  The place is designed to accommodate bicycles, Segways (rentable), and wheelchairs. \n\nI went on a Wednesday and was pleased to find the place uncrowded with no lines, no waiting, and no problem getting the natural photos I wanted.   As others have said,  the outdoor flower gardens, orchid houses, and Royal Pavillion are gorgeous.  There are a multitude of other outdoor displays along the edges that are less impressive, less maintained, and less visited by tourists - ones worth biking through, but not necessarily walking through.  Along the way, you'll find several royal monuments, foreign country display gardens, indoor pavillions, and snack stands, with one larger restaurant in the back near the Royal Project.  Upon entry, you can receive a map if you ask, showing the major displays, as well as the many bathroom locations.\n\nThis park is a photographer's delight - if you come on a sunny day with blue skies.  So wear your hat and don't shun the hot sun since there's plenty of shaded areas to be found along way.  Even the park approach along Ratchapruek Road is noticeably attractive, and as one gets closer, a man-made hill with cool landscaping and a single pinacle tree will warrant your first picture.  And don't rush through the entrance way either without stepping out onto the plaza-like area or climbing the hill where several great pictures can be had of the flags, flowers, fountain, and gate statues.  Inside the park, you'll find brilliant flower colors irresistable for photographing, with the best ones being located in the central area and two adjacent orchid houses.  The impressive Royal Pavillion can be photographed nicely from all sides and angles, including a nice broad view from the nearby hill.  And the viewing tower, which naturally attracted me for some great overview shots of the area?  Not worth the climb.\n\nOverall, I loved this place and easily spent 4 hours here without even reading the many signs or entering the buildings.  I'd suggest dedicating no less than 2-4 hours for your visit.  My 4 star rating reflects an excellent tourist or local attraction that, like most Thai parks, has not been completely maintained.  As they build new and gorgeous displays, some of the periphery areas are being neglected.  Still, such deficiencies won't detract from your enjoyment of the area.",

 'I first visited several years ago when it was the site of an International Flower and Garden Festival when many nations sponsored their traditional gardens. The Park is situated to the south of the city off route 121 (ring road) and is adjacent to the Chiang Mai Night Safari. Today you can still visit these remaining gardens including Japanese, Moroccan, Kenyan, Dutch, Cambodian, Bangladeshi, Chinese and my favorite, the Bhutanese. There are others among the numerous Thai flower bed displays. Several traditional Thai buildings nestle among the gardens,trees and lake. There is a temperate house, a hot house, a beautiful orchid house and exhibition hall. Should you want to "escape" the noise and bustle of the city, then this park makes an ideal peaceful haven to wander and relax in. I advise wearing a hat if it is hot sunshine and should you tire there is a free drop on/drop off shuttle service around the park. Golf buggies can be hired. There is a large car park (20 baht on exit) and entrance is 200 baht. Public service vehicles travel there.',

 "The Royal Park Rajapruek was spectacular when it first opened back in 2006.  It's still quite fabulous in some aspects, but many aspects of the park are in serious decline.  The park is about 15 kilometers from the city center; we managed to negotiate a red truck for 150 baht one way; return by Uber was 220 baht.  The entrance fee is 100 baht for Thais and local residents, and 200 baht for foreigners.  Resident foreigners can probably negotiate the Thai price with a Thai driver's license or ID.  The park is expansive, but there is a free tram service.  We opted instead to rent bikes (60 baht for the full day), which was a brilliant move.  We strongly recommend this option, as it allows you to get around easily while also stopping wherever, whenever, at your own pace.  The highlights of the park are the royal pavilion (fabulous) and the orchid display (out of this world riot of color).  We spent more than four hours at the park, which we felt was well worth it.  The only disappointing aspect was that there are lots of poorly maintained and abandoned buildings and some fenced-off areas no longer available to visitors.  The management of the park will hopefully be able to rally support to revive the neglected parts of the park.",

reviews = [re.sub(r'[^\w\s]','',str(item)) for item in reviews]
In [175]:
from nltk.corpus import stopwords
stopwords = set(stopwords.words('english'))
In [176]:
texts = [[word for word in document.lower().split() if word not in stopwords] for document in reviews]
In [177]:
frequency = defaultdict(int)
for text in texts:
    for token in text:
         frequency[token] += 1

texts = [[token for token in text if frequency[token] > 1] for text in texts]
In [178]:
dictionary = corpora.Dictionary(texts)
In [179]:
print(dictionary)

word_dict = {};
for i in range(NUM_TOPICS):
    words = ldamodel.show_topic(i, topn = 20)
    word_dict['Topic # ' + '{:02d}'.format(i+1)] = [i[0] for i in words]
pd.DataFrame(word_dict)

# Compute Perplexity
print('\nPerplexity: ', ldamodel.log_perplexity(corpus))  # a measure of how good the model is. lower the better.
from gensim.models import CoherenceModel
# Compute Coherence Score
coherence_model_lda = CoherenceModel(model=ldamodel, texts=texts, dictionary=dictionary, coherence='c_v')
coherence_lda = coherence_model_lda.get_coherence()
print('\nCoherence Score: ', coherence_lda)
